  The Dockerfile build failed at the package installation stage (lines 6-18). The error occurred during apt-get install, likely due to missing package sources or unavailable packages. The build hasn't progressed beyond the initial package installation phase.
  next step
  Add apt-get update fix and split the package installation into smaller groups to identify which package is causing the failure. Also add the deadsnakes PPA for Python 3.10 availability on Ubuntu 20.04:
  ```dockerfile
  FROM ubuntu:20.04
  ENV DEBIAN_FRONTEND=noninteractive
  ENV TZ=UTC
  # Update and install software-properties-common first
  RUN apt-get update && apt-get install -y software-properties-common
  # Add deadsnakes PPA for Python 3.10
  RUN add-apt-repository ppa:deadsnakes/ppa && apt-get update
  # Install packages in groups
  RUN apt-get install -y \
      build-essential \
      gcc \
      g++ \
      make
  RUN apt-get install -y \
      git \
      curl \
      wget \
      openssh-client
  RUN apt-get install -y \
      xmlstarlet \
      jq
  RUN apt-get install -y \
      python3.10 \
      python3.10-dev \
      python3.10-venv \
      python3-pip
  RUN rm -rf /var/lib/apt/lists/*
  ```

  ENV PATH="/home/cc/EnvGym/data/acto/.venv/bin:${PATH}"
  CMD ["/bin/bash"]

  #5 32.25  This PPA contains more recent Python versions packaged for Ubuntu.
  #5 32.25 
  #5 32.25 Disclaimer: there's no guarantee of timely updates in case of security problems or other issues. If you want to use them in a security-or-otherwise-critical environment (say, on a production server), you do so at your own risk.
  #5 32.25 
  #5 32.25 Update Note
  #5 32.25 ===========
  #5 32.25 Please use this repository instead of ppa:fkrull/deadsnakes.
  #5 32.25 
  #5 32.25 Reporting Issues
  #5 32.25 ================
  #5 32.25 
  #5 32.25 Issues can be reported in the master issue tracker at:
  #5 32.25 https://github.com/deadsnakes/issues/issues
  #5 32.25 
  #5 32.25 Supported Ubuntu and Python Versions
  #5 32.25 ====================================
  #5 32.25 
  #5 32.25 - Ubuntu 20.04 (focal) Python3.5 - Python3.7, Python3.9 - Python3.13
  #5 32.25 - Ubuntu 22.04 (jammy) Python3.7 - Python3.9, Python3.11 - Python3.13
  #5 32.25 - Ubuntu 24.04 (noble) Python3.7 - Python3.11, Python3.13
  #5 32.25 - Note: Python2.7 (focal, jammy), Python 3.8 (focal), Python 3.10 (jammy), Python3.12 (noble) are not provided by deadsnakes as upstream ubuntu provides those packages.
  #5 32.25 
  #5 32.25 Why some packages aren't built:
  #5 32.25 - Note: for focal, older python versions require libssl<1.1 so they are not currently built
  #5 32.25 - Note: for jammy and noble, older python versions requre libssl<3 so they are not currently built
  #5 32.25 - If you need these, reach out to asottile to set up a private ppa
  #5 32.25 
  #5 32.25 The packages may also work on other versions of Ubuntu or Debian, but that is not tested or supported.
  #5 32.25 
  #5 32.25 Packages
  #5 32.25 ========
  #5 32.25 
  #5 32.25 The packages provided here are loosely based on the debian upstream packages with some modifications to make them more usable as non-default pythons and on ubuntu.  As such, the packages follow debian's patterns and often do not include a full python distribution with just `apt install python#.#`.  Here is a list of packages that may be useful along with the default install:
  #5 32.25 
  #5 32.25 - `python#.#-dev`: includes development headers for building C extensions
  #5 32.25 - `python#.#-venv`: provides the standard library `venv` module
  #5 32.25 - `python#.#-distutils`: provides the standard library `distutils` module
  #5 32.25 - `python#.#-lib2to3`: provides the `2to3-#.#` utility as well as the standard library `lib2to3` module
  #5 32.25 - `python#.#-gdbm`: provides the standard library `dbm.gnu` module
  #5 32.25 - `python#.#-tk`: provides the standard library `tkinter` module
  #5 32.25 
  #5 32.25 Third-Party Python Modules
  #5 32.25 ==========================
  #5 32.25 
  #5 32.25 Python modules in the official Ubuntu repositories are packaged to work with the Python interpreters from the official repositories. Accordingly, they generally won't work with the Python interpreters from this PPA. As an exception, pure-Python modules for Python 3 will work, but any compiled extension modules won't.
  #5 32.25 
  #5 32.25 To install 3rd-party Python modules, you should use the common Python packaging tools.  For an introduction into the Python packaging ecosystem and its tools, refer to the Python Packaging User Guide:
  #5 32.25 https://packaging.python.org/installing/
  #5 32.25 
  #5 32.25 Sources
  #5 32.25 =======
  #5 32.25 The package sources are available at:
  #5 32.25 https://github.com/deadsnakes/

  #5 23.21  This PPA contains more recent Python versions packaged for Ubuntu.
  #5 23.21 
  #5 23.21 Disclaimer: there's no guarantee of timely updates in case of security problems or other issues. If you want to use them in a security-or-otherwise-critical environment (say, on a production server), you do so at your own risk.
  #5 23.21 
  #5 23.21 Update Note
  #5 23.21 ===========
  #5 23.21 Please use this repository instead of ppa:fkrull/deadsnakes.
  #5 23.21 
  #5 23.21 Reporting Issues
  #5 23.21 ================
  #5 23.21 
  #5 23.21 Issues can be reported in the master issue tracker at:
  #5 23.21 https://github.com/deadsnakes/issues/issues
  #5 23.21 
  #5 23.21 Supported Ubuntu and Python Versions
  #5 23.21 ====================================
  #5 23.21 
  #5 23.21 - Ubuntu 20.04 (focal) Python3.5 - Python3.7, Python3.9 - Python3.13
  #5 23.21 - Ubuntu 22.04 (jammy) Python3.7 - Python3.9, Python3.11 - Python3.13
  #5 23.21 - Ubuntu 24.04 (noble) Python3.7 - Python3.11, Python3.13
  #5 23.21 - Note: Python2.7 (focal, jammy), Python 3.8 (focal), Python 3.10 (jammy), Python3.12 (noble) are not provided by deadsnakes as upstream ubuntu provides those packages.
  #5 23.21 
  #5 23.21 Why some packages aren't built:
  #5 23.21 - Note: for focal, older python versions require libssl<1.1 so they are not currently built
  #5 23.21 - Note: for jammy and noble, older python versions requre libssl<3 so they are not currently built
  #5 23.21 - If you need these, reach out to asottile to set up a private ppa
  #5 23.21 
  #5 23.21 The packages may also work on other versions of Ubuntu or Debian, but that is not tested or supported.
  #5 23.21 
  #5 23.21 Packages
  #5 23.21 ========
  #5 23.21 
  #5 23.21 The packages provided here are loosely based on the debian upstream packages with some modifications to make them more usable as non-default pythons and on ubuntu.  As such, the packages follow debian's patterns and often do not include a full python distribution with just `apt install python#.#`.  Here is a list of packages that may be useful along with the default install:
  #5 23.21 
  #5 23.21 - `python#.#-dev`: includes development headers for building C extensions
  #5 23.21 - `python#.#-venv`: provides the standard library `venv` module
  #5 23.21 - `python#.#-distutils`: provides the standard library `distutils` module
  #5 23.21 - `python#.#-lib2to3`: provides the `2to3-#.#` utility as well as the standard library `lib2to3` module
  #5 23.21 - `python#.#-gdbm`: provides the standard library `dbm.gnu` module
  #5 23.21 - `python#.#-tk`: provides the standard library `tkinter` module
  #5 23.21 
  #5 23.21 Third-Party Python Modules
  #5 23.21 ==========================
  #5 23.21 
  #5 23.21 Python modules in the official Ubuntu repositories are packaged to work with the Python interpreters from the official repositories. Accordingly, they generally won't work with the Python interpreters from this PPA. As an exception, pure-Python modules for Python 3 will work, but any compiled extension modules won't.
  #5 23.21 
  #5 23.21 To install 3rd-party Python modules, you should use the common Python packaging tools.  For an introduction into the Python packaging ecosystem and its tools, refer to the Python Packaging User Guide:
  #5 23.21 https://packaging.python.org/installing/
  #5 23.21 
  #5 23.21 Sources
  #5 23.21 =======
  #5 23.21 The package sources are available at:
  #5 23.21 https://github.com/deadsnakes/
  #5 23.21
